Council)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Outer Hebrides</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;h&#39; in &#39;hi&#39;">h</span><span title="/\xc9\x9b/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">\xc9\x9b</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/i\xcb\x90/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">i\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span></span>), also known as the <b>Western Isles</b> (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scottish Gaelic</a>: <i lang="gd">Na h-Eileanan Siar</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Help:IPA/Scottish Gaelic">[n\xc9\x99 \xcb\x88helan\xc9\x99n \xcb\x88\xca\x83i\xc9\x99\xc9\xbe]</a></span> or <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Na h-Eileanan an Iar</i></i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Help:IPA/Scottish Gaelic">[n\xc9\x99\xcb\x88helan\xc9\x99n \xc9\x99\xcb\x88\xc9\xb2i\xc9\x99\xc9\xbe]</a></span>), <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Innse Gall</i></i> ("islands of the strangers") or the <b>Long Isle</b> or the <b>Long Island</b> (Scottish Gaelic: <i lang="gd">An t-Eilean Fada</i>), is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">island chain</a> off the west coast of mainland <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;Note 1&#93;</a></sup> The islands are geographically <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/coextensive" class="extiw" title="wikt:coextensive">coextensive</a> with <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Comhairle_nan_Eilean_Siar" title="Comhairle nan Eilean Siar">Comhairle nan Eilean Siar</a></i>, one of the 32 unitary <a href="/wiki/Council_areas_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Council areas of Scotland">council areas of Scotland</a>. They form part of the archipelago of the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a>, separated from the Scottish mainland and from the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Hebrides" title="Inner Hebrides">Inner Hebrides</a> by the waters of the <a href="/wiki/Minch" class="mw-redirect" title="Minch">Minch</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Little_Minch" class="mw-redirect" title="Little Minch">Little Minch</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_the_Hebrides" title="Sea of the Hebrides">Sea of the Hebrides</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a> is the predominant spoken language, although in a few areas English speakers form a majority.\n</p><p>Most of the islands have a bedrock formed from ancient <a href="/wiki/Metamorphic" class="mw-redirect" title="Metamorphic">metamorphic</a> rocks and the climate is mild and oceanic. The 15 inhabited islands have a total population of 27,000<sup id="cite_ref-population_source_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population_source-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and there are more than 50 substantial uninhabited islands. From <a href="/wiki/Barra_Head" title="Barra Head">Barra Head</a> to the  <a href="/wiki/Butt_of_Lewis" title="Butt of Lewis">Butt of Lewis</a> is roughly 210 kilometres (130&#160;mi).\n</p><p>There are various important prehistoric structures, many of which pre-date the first written references to the islands by <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">Roman and Greek</a> authors. The Western Isles became part of the <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a> kingdom of the <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text"><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Isles" title="Kingdom of the Isles">Su\xc3\xb0reyjar</a></i></i>, which lasted for over 400 years until sovereignty was transferred to Scotland by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Perth" title="Treaty of Perth">Treaty of Perth</a> in 1266. Control of the islands was then held by <a href="/wiki/Scottish_clan" title="Scottish clan">clan</a> chiefs, principal of whom were the <a href="/wiki/Clan_MacLeod" title="Clan MacLeod">MacLeods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clan_Donald" title="Clan Donald">MacDonalds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clan_Mackenzie" title="Clan Mackenzie">Mackenzies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clan_MacNeil" title="Clan MacNeil">MacNeils</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Highland_Clearances" title="Highland Clearances">Highland Clearances</a> of the 19th century had a devastating effect on many communities and it is only in recent years that population levels have ceased to decline. Much of the land is now under local control and commercial activity is based on tourism, <a href="/wiki/Crofting" title="Crofting">crofting</a>, fishing, and weaving.\n</p><p>Sea transport is crucial and a variety of ferry services operate between the islands and to mainland Scotland. Modern navigation systems now minimise the dangers but in the past the stormy seas have claimed many ships. Religion, music and sport are important aspects of local culture, and there are numerous <a href="/wiki/Conservation_designation" title="Conservation designation">designated conservation areas</a> to protect the natural environment.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Flora_and_fauna"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Flora and fauna</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Population"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Population</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Uninhabited_islands"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Uninhabited islands</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Geology"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Geology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Prehistory"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Prehistory</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Etymology"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Norse_control"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Norse control</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Scots_rule"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Scots rule</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#British_era"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">British era</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Politics_and_local_government"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Politics and local government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Scottish_Gaelic_language"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Scottish Gaelic language</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Bus_na_Comhairle"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Bus na Comhairle</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Shipwrecks"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Shipwrecks</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Religion,_culture_and_sport"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Religion, culture and sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Outer_Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Uist.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/South_Uist.jpg/220px-South_Uist.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/South_Uist.jpg/330px-South_Uist.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/South_Uist.jpg/440px-South_Uist.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Uist.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nicolson\'s Leap on the east coast of <a href="/wiki/South_Uist" title="South Uist">South Uist</a>. In the background are Beinn Mh\xc3\xb2r at left, and Hecla on the right.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Outer_Hebrides" title="List of Outer Hebrides">List of Outer Hebrides</a></div>\n<p>The islands form an archipelago whose major islands are <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Harris" title="Lewis and Harris">Lewis and Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Uist" title="North Uist">North Uist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benbecula" title="Benbecula">Benbecula</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Uist" title="South Uist">South Uist</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barra" title="Barra">Barra</a>. Lewis and Harris has an area of 217,898 hectares (841&#160;sq&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-Haswell-Smith_2004_p._289_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haswell-Smith_2004_p._289-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and is the largest island in Scotland and the third largest in the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>, after Great Britain and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It incorporates <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Lewis" title="Isle of Lewis">Lewis</a> in the north and <a href="/wiki/Harris,_Outer_Hebrides" class="mw-redirect" title="Harris, Outer Hebrides">Harris</a> in the south, both of which are frequently referred to as individual islands, although they are connected by land. The island does not have a single name in either English or Gaelic, and is referred to as "Lewis and Harris", "Lewis with Harris", "Harris with Lewis" etc.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_1968_p._13_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson_1968_p._13-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest islands are deeply indented by arms of the sea such as <a href="/wiki/Loch_R%C3%B2g" title="Loch R\xc3\xb2g">Loch R\xc3\xb2g</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loch_Seaforth" title="Loch Seaforth">Loch Seaforth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lochmaddy" title="Lochmaddy">Loch nam Madadh</a>. There are also more than 7,500 freshwater lochs in the Outer Hebrides, about 24% of the total for the whole of Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-SNH_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNH-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> North and South Uist and Lewis in particular have landscapes with a high percentage of fresh water and a maze and complexity of loch shapes. Harris has fewer large bodies of water but has innumerable small lochans. <a href="/wiki/Loch_Langavat" title="Loch Langavat">Loch Langavat</a> on Lewis is 11 kilometres (7&#160;mi) long, and has several large islands in its midst, including <a href="/wiki/Eilean_M%C3%B2r,_Loch_Langavat" title="Eilean M\xc3\xb2r, Loch Langavat">Eilean M\xc3\xb2r</a>. Although Loch Suaineabhal has only 25% of Loch Langavat\'s surface area, it has a mean depth of 33 metres (108&#160;ft) and is the most voluminous on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Of <a href="/wiki/Loch_Sgadabhagh" title="Loch Sgadabhagh">Loch Sgadabhagh</a> on <a href="/wiki/North_Uist" title="North Uist">North Uist</a> it has been said that "there is probably no other loch in Britain which approaches Loch Scadavay in irregularity and complexity of outline."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Loch B\xc3\xac is South Uist\'s largest loch and at 8 kilometres (5&#160;mi) long it all but cuts the island in two.<sup id="cite_ref-OS_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Much of the western coastline of the islands is <a href="/wiki/Machair_(geography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Machair (geography)">machair</a>, a fertile low-lying dune pastureland.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Lewis is comparatively flat, and largely consists of treeless moors of blanket <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a>. The highest eminence is Mealisval at 574&#160;m (1,883&#160;ft) in the south west. Most of <a href="/wiki/Harris,_Outer_Hebrides" class="mw-redirect" title="Harris, Outer Hebrides">Harris</a> is mountainous, with large areas of exposed rock and <a href="/wiki/Clisham" title="Clisham">Clisham</a>, the archipelago\'s only <a href="/wiki/Corbett_Top" class="mw-redirect" title="Corbett Top">Corbett</a>, reaches 799&#160;m (2,621&#160;ft) in height.<sup id="cite_ref-Thom14_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thom14-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Haswell-Smith_2004_p._289_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haswell-Smith_2004_p._289-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> North and South Uist and Benbecula (sometimes collectively referred to as <a href="/wiki/The_Uists" class="mw-redirect" title="The Uists">The Uists</a>) have sandy beaches and wide cultivated areas of machair to the west and virtually uninhabited mountainous areas to the east. The highest peak here is <a href="/wiki/Beinn_Mh%C3%B2r_(South_Uist)" title="Beinn Mh\xc3\xb2r (South Uist)">Beinn Mh\xc3\xb2r</a> at 620 metres (2,034&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The Uists and their immediate outliers have a combined area of 74,540 hectares (288&#160;sq&#160;mi). This includes the Uists themselves and the islands linked to them by causeways and bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Barra is 5,875 hectares (23&#160;sq&#160;mi) in extent and has a rugged interior, surrounded by machair and extensive beaches.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The scenic qualities of the islands are reflected in the fact that three of Scotland\'s forty <a href="/wiki/National_scenic_area_(Scotland)" title="National scenic area (Scotland)">national scenic areas</a> (NSAs) are located here. The national scenic areas are defined so as to identify areas of exceptional scenery and to ensure its protection from inappropriate development,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and are considered to represent the type of scenic beauty "popularly associated with Scotland and for which it is renowned".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The three NSA within the Outer Hebridies are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/South_Lewis,_Harris_and_North_Uist_National_Scenic_Area" title="South Lewis, Harris and North Uist National Scenic Area">South Lewis, Harris and North Uist National Scenic Area</a> covers the mountainous south west of <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Lewis" title="Isle of Lewis">Lewis</a>, all of <a href="/wiki/Harris,_Outer_Hebrides" class="mw-redirect" title="Harris, Outer Hebrides">Harris</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sound_of_Harris" title="Sound of Harris">Sound of Harris</a> and the northern part of <a href="/wiki/North_Uist" title="North Uist">North Uist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>An area of the south west coast of <a href="/wiki/South_Uist" title="South Uist">South Uist</a> is designated as the <i>South Uist Machair National Scenic Area</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The archipelago of <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St Kilda</a> is also listed as an NSA, alongside many other conservation designations.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Outer_Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flora_and_fauna_of_the_Outer_Hebrides" title="Flora and fauna of the Outer Hebrides">Flora and fauna of the Outer Hebrides</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg/220px-Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg/330px-Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg/440px-Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="429" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benbecula_Ruabhal_View.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The open landscapes of <a href="/wiki/Benbecula" title="Benbecula">Benbecula</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baghmor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Baghmor.jpg/220px-Baghmor.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Baghmor.jpg/330px-Baghmor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Baghmor.jpg/440px-Baghmor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="431" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baghmor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">B\xc3\xa0gh M\xc3\xb2r</i>, <a href="/wiki/Grimsay" title="Grimsay">Grimsay</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Much of the archipelago is a protected habitat, including both the islands and the surrounding waters. There are 53 <a href="/wiki/Sites_of_Special_Scientific_Interest" class="mw-redirect" title="Sites of Special Scientific Interest">Sites of Special Scientific Interest</a> of which the largest are Loch an Duin, North Uist (15,100 hectares (37,000 acres)) and North Harris (12,700 hectares (31,000 acres)).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Uist" title="South Uist">South Uist</a> is considered the best place in the UK for the aquatic plant <a href="/wiki/Najas_flexilis" title="Najas flexilis">Slender Naiad</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/European_Protected_Species" title="European Protected Species">European Protected Species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There has been considerable controversy over <a href="/wiki/European_hedgehog" title="European hedgehog">hedgehogs</a> on the Uists. Hedgehogs are not native to the islands, but were introduced in the 1970s to reduce garden pests. Their spread posed a threat to the eggs of ground nesting wading birds. In 2003 Scottish Natural Heritage undertook culls of hedgehogs in the area, but these were halted in 2007; trapped animals are now relocated to the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nationally important populations of breeding waders are present in the Outer Hebrides, including <a href="/wiki/Common_redshank" title="Common redshank">common redshank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dunlin" title="Dunlin">dunlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_lapwing" title="Northern lapwing">lapwing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ringed_plover" class="mw-redirect" title="Ringed plover">ringed plover</a>. The islands also provide a habitat for other important species such as <a href="/wiki/Corn_crake" title="Corn crake">corncrake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hen_harrier" title="Hen harrier">hen harrier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_otter" class="mw-redirect" title="European otter">otter</a>. Offshore, <a href="/wiki/Basking_shark" title="Basking shark">basking shark</a> and various species of whale and dolphin can often be seen,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and the remoter islands\' seabird populations are of international significance. <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St Kilda</a> has 60,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Northern_gannet" title="Northern gannet">northern gannets</a>, amounting to 24% of the world population; 49,000&#160;breeding pairs of <a href="/wiki/Leach%27s_storm-petrel" class="mw-redirect" title="Leach&#39;s storm-petrel">Leach\'s petrel</a>, up to 90% of the European population; and 136,000&#160;pairs of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_puffin" title="Atlantic puffin">puffin</a> and 67,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Northern_fulmar" title="Northern fulmar">northern fulmar</a> pairs, about 30% and 13% of the respective UK totals.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mingulay" title="Mingulay">Mingulay</a> is an important breeding ground for <a href="/wiki/Razorbill" title="Razorbill">razorbills</a>, with 9,514&#160;pairs, 6.3% of the European population.<sup id="cite_ref-NTSbirds_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NTSbirds-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bumblebee" title="Bumblebee">bumblebee</a> <a href="/wiki/Bombus_jonellus" title="Bombus jonellus"><i>Bombus jonellus</i> var. <i>hebridensis</i></a> is <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> to the Hebrides and there are local variants of the <a href="/wiki/Dark_green_fritillary" title="Dark green fritillary">dark green fritillary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green-veined_white" title="Green-veined white">green-veined white</a> butterflies.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda_wren" title="St Kilda wren">St Kilda wren</a> is a subspecies of <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_wren" title="Eurasian wren">wren</a> whose range is confined to the islands whose name it bears.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Outer_Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LewsCastle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/LewsCastle.jpg/220px-LewsCastle.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/LewsCastle.jpg/330px-LewsCastle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/LewsCastle.jpg/440px-LewsCastle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LewsCastle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lews_Castle" title="Lews Castle">Lews Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stornoway" title="Stornoway">Stornoway</a></div></div></div>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Historical population</th></tr><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Percent change">\xc2\xb1%</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1861 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">36,319</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x80\x94&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1901 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">46,172</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+27.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1951 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">35,591</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x9222.9%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1961 </th><td style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1991 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">29,600</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x923.6%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2001 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">26,502</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x9210.5%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2011 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">27,684</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+4.5%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left"><sup id="cite_ref-NRS_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRS-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The islands\' total population was 26,502 at the 2001 census, and the 2011 figure was 27,684.<sup id="cite_ref-NRS_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRS-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> During the same period <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scottish_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Scottish islands">Scottish island</a> populations as a whole grew by 4% to 103,702.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The largest settlement in the Outer Hebrides is <a href="/wiki/Stornoway" title="Stornoway">Stornoway</a> on Lewis,<sup id="cite_ref-Pop11_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pop11-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GRO_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GRO-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> which has a population of about 8,100.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to the major North Ford (<i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Oitir Mh\xc3\xb2r</i></i>) and South Ford causeways that connect North Uist to Benbecula via the northern of the <a href="/wiki/Grimsay" title="Grimsay">Grimsays</a>, and another causeway from Benbecula to South Uist, several other islands are linked by smaller causeways or bridges. <a href="/wiki/Great_Bernera" title="Great Bernera">Great Bernera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scalpay,_Outer_Hebrides" title="Scalpay, Outer Hebrides">Scalpay</a> have bridge connections to Lewis and Harris respectively, with causeways linking <a href="/wiki/Baleshare" title="Baleshare">Baleshare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berneray,_North_Uist" class="mw-redirect" title="Berneray, North Uist">Berneray</a> to North Uist; <a href="/wiki/Eriskay" title="Eriskay">Eriskay</a> to South Uist; <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Flodaigh" title="Flodaigh">Flodaigh</a></i>, <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Fraoch-Eilean" title="Fraoch-Eilean">Fraoch-Eilean</a></i> and the southern <a href="/wiki/Grimsay,_South_East_Benbecula" class="mw-redirect" title="Grimsay, South East Benbecula">Grimsay</a> to Benbecula; and <a href="/wiki/Vatersay" title="Vatersay">Vatersay</a> to Barra.<sup id="cite_ref-OS_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OS-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-calmac_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-calmac-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Thus means that all the inhabited islands are now connected to at least one other island by a land transport route.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scots_Gaelic_speakers_in_the_2011_census.png" class="image"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Scots_Gaelic_speakers_in_the_2011_census.png/270px-Scots_Gaelic_speakers_in_the_2011_census.png 1.5x, speakers in Scotland (2011)</div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Island\n</th>\n<th>Gaelic name\n</th>\n<th>2011 population<sup id="cite_ref-NRS_34-2" style="display:none" class="sortkey">7004276840000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>27,684\n</td>\n<td><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7004265020000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>26,502\n</td>\n<td>52% (14,248)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uninhabited_islands">Uninhabited islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Outer_Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Uninhabited islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_south_from_Heaval.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/View_south_from_Heaval.jpg/220px-View_south_from_Heaval.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/View_south_from_Heaval.jpg/330px-View_south_from_Heaval.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/View_south_from_Heaval.jpg/440px-View_south_from_Heaval.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_south_from_Heaval.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the <a href="/wiki/Barra_Isles" title="Barra Isles">Barra Isles</a> from <a href="/wiki/Heaval" title="Heaval">Heaval</a>. The village of <a href="/wiki/Castlebay" title="Castlebay">Castlebay</a> is in the foreground, with <a href="/wiki/Vatersay" title="Vatersay">Vatersay</a>, and the uninhabited islands of <a href="/wiki/Sandray" title="Sandray">Sandray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pabbay,_Barra,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Pabbay, Barra, Scotland">Pabbay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mingulay" title="Mingulay">Mingulay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barra_Head" title="Barra Head">Berneray</a> beyond.</div></div></div>\n<p>There are more than fifty uninhabited islands greater in size than 40 hectares (99 acres) in the Outer Hebrides, including the <a href="/wiki/Barra_Isles" title="Barra Isles">Barra Isles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flannan_Isles" title="Flannan Isles">Flannan Isles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monach_Islands" title="Monach Islands">Monach Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shiant_Isles" title="Shiant Isles">Shiant Isles</a> and the islands of <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Loch R\xc3\xb2g</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In common with the other main island chains of Scotland, many of the more remote islands were abandoned during the 19th and 20th centuries, in some cases after continuous habitation since the prehistoric period. More than 35 such islands have been identified in the Outer Hebrides alone.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On Barra Head, for example, <a href="/wiki/Historic_Scotland" title="Historic Scotland">Historic Scotland</a> have identified eighty-three archaeological sites on the island, the majority being of a pre-medieval date. In the 18th century the population was over fifty, but the last native islanders had left by 1931.  The island became completely uninhabited by 1980 with the automation of the lighthouse.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the smaller islands continue to contribute to modern culture. The "<a href="/wiki/Mingulay_Boat_Song" title="Mingulay Boat Song">Mingulay Boat Song</a>", although evocative of island life, was written after the abandonment of the island in 1938<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Taransay" title="Taransay">Taransay</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Castaway_2000" title="Castaway 2000">Castaway 2000</a></i>. Others have played a part in Scottish history. On 4 May 1746, the "Young Pretender" <a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles Edward Stuart</a> hid on <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Eilean_Liubhaird" title="Eilean Liubhaird">Eilean Liubhaird</a></i> with some of his men for four days whilst <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> vessels patrolled the Minch.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Smaller isles and <a href="/wiki/Skerry" title="Skerry">skerries</a> and other island groups pepper the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic">North Atlantic</a> surrounding the main islands. Some are not geologically part of the Outer Hebrides, but are administratively and in most cases culturally, part of <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Comhairle nan Eilean Siar</i>. 73 kilometres (45&#160;mi) to the west of Lewis lies <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St Kilda</a>, now uninhabited except for a small military base.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> A similar distance to the north of Lewis are <a href="/wiki/North_Rona" title="North Rona">North Rona</a> and <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Sula_Sgeir" title="Sula Sgeir">Sula Sgeir</a></i>, two small and remote islands. While Rona used to support a small population who grew grain and raised cattle, <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Sula Sgeir</i> is an inhospitable rock.  Thousands of <a href="/wiki/Northern_gannet" title="Northern gannet">northern gannets</a> nest here, and by special arrangement some of their young, known as <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">gugas</i></i> are harvested annually by the men of <a href="/wiki/Ness,_Outer_Hebrides" class="mw-redirect" title="Ness, Outer Hebrides">Ness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The status of <a href="/wiki/Rockall" title="Rockall">Rockall</a>, which is 367 kilometres (228&#160;mi) to the west of North Uist and which the <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Rockall_Act_1972" title="Island of Rockall Act 1972">Island of Rockall Act 1972</a> decreed to be a part of the Western Isles, remains a matter of international dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Outer_Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hebridean_Terrane.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Hebridean_Terrane.png/220px-Hebridean_Terrane.png" width="220" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Hebridean_Terrane.png/330px-Hebridean_Terrane.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Hebridean_Terrane.png/440px-Hebridean_Terrane.png 2x" data-file-width="1218" data-file-height="1350" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hebridean_Terrane.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geological map of the <a href="/wiki/Hebridean_Terrane" title="Hebridean Terrane">Hebridean Terrane</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Most of the islands have a bedrock formed from <a href="/wiki/Lewisian_complex" title="Lewisian complex">Lewisian gneiss</a>. These are amongst the oldest rocks in Europe, having been formed in the <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">Precambrian</a> period up to three billion years ago. In addition to the Outer Hebrides, they form basement deposits on the Scottish mainland west of the <a href="/wiki/Moine_Thrust_Belt" title="Moine Thrust Belt">Moine Thrust</a> and on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Coll" title="Coll">Coll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tiree" title="Tiree">Tiree</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> These rocks are largely igneous in origin, mixed with metamorphosed <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quartzite" title="Quartzite">quartzite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mica_schist" class="mw-redirect" title="Mica schist">mica schist</a> and intruded by later basaltic <a href="/wiki/Dyke_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dyke (geology)">dykes</a> and granite magma.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The gneiss\'s delicate pink colours are exposed throughout the islands and it is sometimes referred to by geologists as "The Old Boy".<sup id="cite_ref-Murray_1966_p._2_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray_1966_p._2-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;Note 3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Granite intrusions are found in the parish of <a href="/wiki/Barvas" title="Barvas">Barvas</a> in west Lewis, and another forms the summit plateau of the mountain <a href="/wiki/Roineabhal" title="Roineabhal">Roineabhal</a> in Harris. The granite here is <a href="/wiki/Anorthosite" title="Anorthosite">anorthosite</a>, and is similar in composition to rocks found in the mountains of the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>. There are relatively small outcrops of <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a> sandstone at <a href="/wiki/Broad_Bay_(Western_Isles)" title="Broad Bay (Western Isles)">Broad Bay</a> near Stornoway. The Shiant Isles and St Kilda are formed from much later tertiary <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a> and basalt and <a href="/wiki/Gabbro" title="Gabbro">gabbros</a> respectively. The sandstone at Broad Bay was once thought to be <a href="/wiki/Torridonian" title="Torridonian">Torridonian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Old_Red_Sandstone" title="Old Red Sandstone">Old Red Sandstone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_1968_p._13_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson_1968_p._13-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Outer_Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Outer Hebrides have a cool temperate climate that is remarkably mild and steady for such a northerly <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a>, due to the influence of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Current" title="North Atlantic Current">North Atlantic Current</a>. The average temperature for the year is 6&#160;\xc2\xb0C (44&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in January and 14&#160;\xc2\xb0C (57&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in summer. The average annual rainfall in Lewis is 1,100 millimetres (43&#160;in) and sunshine hours range from 1,100 to 1,200 per year. The summer days are relatively long and May to August is the driest period.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Winds are a key feature of the climate and even in summer there are almost constant breezes. According to the writer <a href="/wiki/W._H._Murray" title="W. H. Murray">W. H. Murray</a> if a visitor asks an islander for a weather forecast "he will not, like a mainlander answer dry, wet or sunny, but quote you a figure from the <a href="/wiki/Beaufort_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Beaufort Scale">Beaufort Scale</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> There are gales one day in six at the <a href="/wiki/Butt_of_Lewis" title="Butt of Lewis">Butt of Lewis</a> and small fish are blown onto the grass on top of 190&#160;metre (620&#160;ft) high cliffs at <a href="/wiki/Barra_Head" title="Barra Head">Barra Head</a> during winter storms.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Outer_Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Calanais_Standing_Stones_20090610_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Calanais_Standing_Stones_20090610_01.jpg/220px-Calanais_Standing_Stones_20090610_01.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Calanais_Standing_Stones_20090610_01.jpg/330px-Calanais_Standing_Stones_20090610_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Calanais_Standing_Stones_20090610_01.jpg/440px-Calanais_Standing_Stones_20090610_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="486" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Calanais_Standing_Stones_20090610_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Callanish_Stones" title="Callanish Stones">Callanish Stones</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Hebrides were originally settled in the <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic era</a> and have a diversity of important <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">prehistoric</a> sites. <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Eilean_D%C3%B2mhnuill" title="Eilean D\xc3\xb2mhnuill">Eilean D\xc3\xb2mhnuill</a></i> in <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Loch Olabhat</i> on <a href="/wiki/North_Uist" title="North Uist">North Uist</a> was constructed around 3200\xe2\x80\x932800 BC and may be Scotland\'s earliest <a href="/wiki/Crannog" title="Crannog">crannog</a> (a type of artificial island).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Callanish_Stones" title="Callanish Stones">Callanish Stones</a>, dating from about 2900 BC, are the finest example of a <a href="/wiki/Stone_circle" title="Stone circle">stone circle</a> in Scotland, the 13 primary <a href="/wiki/Monolith" title="Monolith">monoliths</a> of between one and five metres high creating a circle about 13 metres (43&#160;ft) in diameter.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Cladh_Hallan" title="Cladh Hallan">Cladh Hallan</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/South_Uist" title="South Uist">South Uist</a>, the only site in the UK where prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Mummy" title="Mummy">mummies</a> have been found, and the impressive ruins of <a href="/wiki/Dun_Carloway" title="Dun Carloway">Dun Carloway</a> <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text"><a href="/wiki/Broch" title="Broch">broch</a></i> on Lewis both date from the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Outer_Hebrides&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barra_Head_Lighthouse_cliffs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A small white building is barely visible on top of dark and imposing cliffs with deep blue water at their base." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Barra_Head_Lighthouse_cliffs.jpg/180px-Barra_Head_Lighthouse_cliffs.jpg" width="180" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Barra_Head_Lighthouse_cliffs.jpg/270px-Barra_Head_Lighthouse_cliffs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Barra_Head_Lighthouse_cliffs.jpg/360px-Barra_Head_Lighthouse_cliffs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barra_Head_Lighthouse_cliffs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "<a href="/wiki/Lewisian_complex" title="Lewisian complex">Old Boy</a>" \xe2\x80\x94 the <a href="/wiki/Gneiss" title="Gneiss">gneiss</a> cliffs of <i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Sloc na B\xc3\xa8iste</i>, <a href="/wiki/Barra_Head" title="Barra Head">Barra Head</a>, the southernmost point of the Outer Hebrides</div></div></div>\n<table class="collapsible infobox collapsed" style="width:280px; title="Scots Gaelic">Scots Gaelic</a>:</td>\n<td><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">Oitir Mh\xc3\xb2r</i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Pronunciation:</td>\n<td><small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Help:IPA/Scottish Gaelic">[\xcb\x88\xc9\x94\xca\xb0t\xca\xb2\xc9\xaa\xc9\xbe\xca\xb2 \xcb\x88vo\xcb\x90\xc9\xbe]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Oitirmhor.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png
